  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5194394-shawna"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1546233249i/5194394._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5194394-shawna">Shawna</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This book was included in our pre-k homeschool curriculum. I started reading it to my son when he was 4 and he enjoyed it and asked some questions but<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This book was included in our pre-k homeschool curriculum. I started reading it to my son when he was 4 and he enjoyed it and asked some questions but the pages have quite a few words and labels on them so I couldn't keep his interest for very long. So I paused. Now, at 5.5, he definitely understood more, enjoyed it more and asked me to keep reading. I think the perfect age range would be age 5+ (kindergarten and up). My personal opinion.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2818939614" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2818939614" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2818939614?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553520590" href="/book/show/23395692-richard-scarry-s-what-do-people-do-all-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=language-learning">language-learning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=cars">cars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2818939614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18313317355776643877">While Richard Scarry's <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> definitely is engagingly entertaining, full of details upon details and thus both textually and illustratively informative (and albeit I do also have fond memories using a school library copy in grade four to practice my English vocabulary), personally I have always found <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> as much too frenetic and too in-your-face busy for my tastes (and most definitely with TOO MUCH of an emphasis on physical work, and especially on veh</span>
  <span id="freeText18313317355776643877" style="display:none">While Richard Scarry's <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> definitely is engagingly entertaining, full of details upon details and thus both textually and illustratively informative (and albeit I do also have fond memories using a school library copy in grade four to practice my English vocabulary), personally I have always found <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> as much too frenetic and too in-your-face busy for my tastes (and most definitely with TOO MUCH of an emphasis on physical work, and especially on vehicles and machinery). In other words, I usually do tend to always consider Richard Scarry's <u>Best Word Book Ever</u> rather more balanced with regard to presenting an acceptable combination of home and public life (and thus also not as overtly and joyously extroverted as <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u>) and yes indeed, that <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> is in my opinion simply and totally just a bit too constantly into getting up and going, too celebratory and supportive of the so-called modern rat race. <br /><br />And albeit that even as a child of ten when I was using <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> to increase my English vocabulary I found the emphasis on especially all work and no play, on modernity or bust so to speak a wee bit uncomfortable and unnatural, now as an older (much more introverted) adult reader revisiting Richard Scarry for the first time since 1976, I actually do consider it quite majorly problematic in and of itself that <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> really and unfortunately (at least in my opinion) overly focusses on people working, that the book so blatantly and one-sidedly celebrates and supports without any type of criticism whatsoever technology, vehicles, being out and busily with a rather total and overt Protestant work ethic rushing and achieving, while life itself, while quietude, sitting back and thinking, reading, pondering the world, while any kind of activity that seems to be based on reflectiveness and using one's mind feels to and for me at best rather ignored in <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> as being unimportant or at least rather insignificant to and for one's daily routines and one's work habits (one's modern life). <br /><br />And yes, even Richard Scarry's signature accompanying illustrations, while they do possess colour and charm, they are equally in <u>What Do People Do All Day?</u> much too frenetically busy for my aesthetic tastes and philosophy and for the most part also just too unapologetically pro modern technology, pro machinery, using vehicles day in and day out with no consideration and promotion of alternatives (and certainly not ever really in any manner presenting any consideration and questions regarding potential issues of pollution, over-consumption and that too many vehicles might strain resources and have the tendency to wreak havoc on the environment and natural ecosystems).</span>
  <a data-text-id="18313317355776643877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14092869445714541023" style="display:none">I think I spent more hours in relationship with this book than maybe any other in my life, other than some spiritual texts.<br /><br />I was fascinated by all the things people did for jobs, all the detail in the illustrations, the sense of humor inherent in all of it. I would gaze at just one page for something like a half-hour, like it was television, but the stories were ones I was telling myself about the characters.<br /><br />Soon I began drawing the characters (pigs were my favorite), first copying exactly and then getting the feel for how a pig was "constructed" and drawing the characters in new poses, outfits, etc. One of the first "lightbulbs" to go off for me about how much I loved to draw and paint.<br /><br />So thank you Richard Scarry!!</span>

<div id="review_3444332618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3444332618" />
    <a title="Gerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry"><img alt="Gerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580749249p2/1525599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3444332618?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerry" href="/user/show/1525599-gerry">Gerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3444332618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13878987140731965808">I saw this book on my shelves the other day when I was trying (desperately) to get some semblance of order in things and the title struck me as appropriate for the situation we have recently been in - and still are!. I do admire Richard Scarry's books, particularly his illustrations for they are all full of energy but if he were writing this book today he would have to change the jobs that people are doing, because, apart from the indoor jobs, none of the others would be taking place!<br/><br/>It is a lov</span>
  <span id="freeText13878987140731965808" style="display:none">I saw this book on my shelves the other day when I was trying (desperately) to get some semblance of order in things and the title struck me as appropriate for the situation we have recently been in - and still are!. I do admire Richard Scarry's books, particularly his illustrations for they are all full of energy but if he were writing this book today he would have to change the jobs that people are doing, because, apart from the indoor jobs, none of the others would be taking place!<br /><br />It is a lovely book, all 63 pages are packed with illustrations that fit the bill perfectly. He begins by giving us a double page spread of the various jobs that are being undertaken and then telling us 'Everyone is a worker' - really? Well in Richard Scarry's world, yes, there is massive activity on every page!<br /><br />There's a family building a new house and every aspect of doing so is covered in great detail. Mailing a letter is a lot simpler but still there are three pages explaining what happens when this activity is undertaken.Firemen attending a fire, patients visiting a hospital, a trip on a train, diesel-electric type, and the story of seeds prove very detailed with Alfalfa in the latter growing the best ever and largest corn on the cob.<br /><br />Wood and how we use it and building a new road are interestingly covered, a voyage on a ship is full of activity and finally where bread comes from reminds me of my Dad as a master baker when I used to go and play in the bakehouse and get covered in flour! Just like my Dad's bread, it did taste good!<br /><br />Colourful, funny and very easy to read and follow, Richard Scarry lives up to his reputation with the illustrations brilliantly complementing the activities.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13878987140731965808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/271355-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363406354p2/271355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2141867997?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/271355-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553520590" href="/book/show/23395692-richard-scarry-s-what-do-people-do-all-day">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/271355-jess?shelf=picture-books">picture-books</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141867997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12996562262415374091">September 2017 - I have a love/hate relationship with Richard Scarry. I love the details, the labels, the explanations of all kinds of things kids are interested in. But ugh, despite some improvements to the illustrations, there are still some super, super sexist stories in here, and I couldn't make it all the way through as a read-aloud - things that were too fundamental to the story to change on the fly. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Laura (Book Scrounger)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33792597-laura-book-scrounger"><img alt="Laura (Book Scrounger)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541274882p2/33792597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617808094?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura (Book Scrounger)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura (Book Scrounger)" href="/user/show/33792597-laura-book-scrounger">Laura (Book Scrounger)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33792597-laura-book-scrounger?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33792597-laura-book-scrounger?shelf=sonlight-curriculum">sonlight-curriculum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33792597-laura-book-scrounger?shelf=00-pre-k">00-pre-k</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617808094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7568917981993718453">This is probably one of my four-year-old's favorite books. It takes a long time to read because the text is all over the pages (which can be nice because that helps it describe things more specifically), but he really enjoys seeing all of the different workers, especially the lumberjacks, farmers, and construction workers. He tells me that when he grows up, he wants to be "a worker"!<br/><br/>There is a fair amount of silliness as is typical in Busytown, and of course, anthropomorphic animals, but it seem</span>
  <span id="freeText7568917981993718453" style="display:none">This is probably one of my four-year-old's favorite books. It takes a long time to read because the text is all over the pages (which can be nice because that helps it describe things more specifically), but he really enjoys seeing all of the different workers, especially the lumberjacks, farmers, and construction workers. He tells me that when he grows up, he wants to be "a worker"!<br /><br />There is a fair amount of silliness as is typical in Busytown, and of course, anthropomorphic animals, but it seems that most of the professions presented here are fairly accurate. It gives kids a good idea of some of the work that many jobs entail. <br /><br />The main downside for me is that it's rather dated -- not just in terms of steam shovels and construction procedures, but also gender equality. I'm sure it was probably just a reflection of its time, but the majority of workers shown here are male, with the exception of a few nurses. Women are mostly portrayed as housewives (and in one case, we are told her husband gave her a new dress because she "earned" it by "taking such good care of the house.").<br /><br />I'm glad Sonlight also includes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2280534.Things_People_Do" title="Things People Do by Anne Civardi" rel="nofollow noopener">Things People Do</a> with this one in their curriculum, because that one seems a lot more balanced to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7568917981993718453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_112072239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112072239" />
    <a title="Shanna Gonzalez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1533441-shanna-gonzalez"><img alt="Shanna Gonzalez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1221561813p2/1533441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112072239?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shanna Gonzalez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shanna Gonzalez" href="/user/show/1533441-shanna-gonzalez">Shanna Gonzalez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1533441-shanna-gonzalez?shelf=children-00-04">children-00-04</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112072239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11207798129310793619">Richard Scarry had a tremendous gift for telling stories that, while simple in plot, are rich in visual detail so that, having been read aloud once, they provide hours of entertainment for prereaders to enjoy at their leisure. His lively, fill-up-the-page artwork and classic sense of humor have endeared him to children for over fifty years.<br/><br/>In this book, Scarry introduces individual citizens of Busytown, then tells short stories about specific projects they are involved in: building a house, mail</span>
  <span id="freeText11207798129310793619" style="display:none">Richard Scarry had a tremendous gift for telling stories that, while simple in plot, are rich in visual detail so that, having been read aloud once, they provide hours of entertainment for prereaders to enjoy at their leisure. His lively, fill-up-the-page artwork and classic sense of humor have endeared him to children for over fifty years.<br /><br />In this book, Scarry introduces individual citizens of Busytown, then tells short stories about specific projects they are involved in: building a house, mailing a letter, putting out a fire, visiting the hospital, riding a train, growing a crop, lumberjacking and processing wood, building a road, taking an ocean voyage, and making bread. By interweaving these individual stories, he shows how greater social process work together in industrial society. Each story demonstrates the value of work, both for the individuals who perform it and those who enjoy its effects. It's a wonderfully orienting book, helping even very young children understand the interworkings of their society.<br /><br />This abridged edition is easy to find, but disappointingly, the unabridged version (which includes a stay-at-home mom, policeman, water treatment processes, and electric plant) has become a collector's item.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11207798129310793619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1814567799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814567799" />
    <a title="Robbie Cheadle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59457436-robbie-cheadle"><img alt="Robbie Cheadle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544722792p2/59457436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814567799?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robbie Cheadle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robbie Cheadle" href="/user/show/59457436-robbie-cheadle">Robbie Cheadle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814567799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11293127962997107399">I absolutely love Richard Scarry books. The stories are such fun and are also informative and the pictures are amazing. What do people do all day? is packed with interesting illustrations and stories about all sorts of workers including a farmer, a mother, the captain of a ship and a police sergeant. All of the workers are depicted as different animals and there are all sorts of little sub-stories going on in the background of each story. These sub-stories are very amusing. The pictures are very</span>
  <span id="freeText11293127962997107399" style="display:none">I absolutely love Richard Scarry books. The stories are such fun and are also informative and the pictures are amazing. What do people do all day? is packed with interesting illustrations and stories about all sorts of workers including a farmer, a mother, the captain of a ship and a police sergeant. All of the workers are depicted as different animals and there are all sorts of little sub-stories going on in the background of each story. These sub-stories are very amusing. The pictures are very busy but they are full of action and you can spend ages looking at and discussing the pictures with your child. The pictures will also give you a good giggle as there are also a host of little sub-plots going on in the illustrations. This book is an enjoyable way of teaching children about fires, going to hospital and a train trip as well as how people use wood and build roads. I remember reading Richard Scarry's books when I was young and then I read them to both my boys, separately due to the age gap. I am now reading them to my nieces and I still enjoy them thoroughly. I would recommend this book for children aged 3 and upwards if mom or dad is reading. Children from aged 9 and upwards can read these books themselves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11293127962997107399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3563047131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9413375079075302290">This was recommended to me by a labor historian I respect who praised it for implicitly acknowledging that all kinds of jobs and work are equally important to society.<br/><br/>The diagrams of waterwheels and gears and underground pipes are enchanting.<br/><br/>However, my edition at least has not been updated, like some Scarry books, to include women. The first woman with a job outside the home appears on page 43, she is a nurse, the mom does everything at home, etc. There were not even teachers in this book. For </span>
  <span id="freeText9413375079075302290" style="display:none">This was recommended to me by a labor historian I respect who praised it for implicitly acknowledging that all kinds of jobs and work are equally important to society.<br /><br />The diagrams of waterwheels and gears and underground pipes are enchanting.<br /><br />However, my edition at least has not been updated, like some Scarry books, to include women. The first woman with a job outside the home appears on page 43, she is a nurse, the mom does everything at home, etc. There were not even teachers in this book. For this reason I can't make it a staple for my daughter.<br /><br />I would also have liked to see some examples of people who work in offices! Because that's the real question, isn't it?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11948523896551263683">I thought I vividly remembered this book from my childhood, but on an adult second reading I only vividly remember through about page 9. My mom would always choose this book as the last bedtime book on those holdout nights when I resisted sleep. Its long and kindof dry, but it has its good points too.<br/><br/>This book is full of vocabulary that kids are sure to hear everyday and simple explinations for what the things are. The illustrations are funny and detailed. Once you learn all the characters, its </span>
  <span id="freeText11948523896551263683" style="display:none">I thought I vividly remembered this book from my childhood, but on an adult second reading I only vividly remember through about page 9. My mom would always choose this book as the last bedtime book on those holdout nights when I resisted sleep. Its long and kindof dry, but it has its good points too.<br /><br />This book is full of vocabulary that kids are sure to hear everyday and simple explinations for what the things are. The illustrations are funny and detailed. Once you learn all the characters, its fun to play I spy and find them all. <br /><br />This book is so dense, it has many purposes- vocab, entertainment, bore to sleep- a great one for your child's personal library. <br /><br />Update:<br />Now I am reading this book with my son, and I truly appreciate how the book has been updated, without adding technology.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14061999118627810832">A timeless children's classic. I learned to read at a very early age largely on account of this book. Not only that, I still own the very copy of <i>What Do People Do All Day</i> I cut my literary teeth on. It's been loved to near death: the binding, long since disintegrated, now consists of three loops of candy-striped yarn, and the outside edges of most of the pages are in tatters. Yet Huckle and his companions live on, as industrious and helpful as they were forty years past.<br/><br/>Richard Scarry's works n</span>
  <span id="freeText14061999118627810832" style="display:none">A timeless children's classic. I learned to read at a very early age largely on account of this book. Not only that, I still own the very copy of <i>What Do People Do All Day</i> I cut my literary teeth on. It's been loved to near death: the binding, long since disintegrated, now consists of three loops of candy-striped yarn, and the outside edges of most of the pages are in tatters. Yet Huckle and his companions live on, as industrious and helpful as they were forty years past.<br /><br />Richard Scarry's works nicely complement the less complicated but slightly deranged Dr. Seuss staples. Scarry's humor is more subtle, with most of the funny stuff going on in the background, more slapstick and less bizarre than Seuss's.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087495091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12020507696607745750">One of my favorite books of all time! What Do People Do All Day? is a picture book written and illustrated by Richard Scarry. It’s appropriate for children aged 3-7. In 2012, the book won the Scholastic Parent and Child 100 Greatest Books for Kids. The pages show the town of Busytown and the places people go and work such as a paper mill, construction site, and hospital. The pictures are incredibly detailed and full of recognizable Richard Scarry characters. <br/><br/>There are so many ways in which to ut</span>
  <span id="freeText12020507696607745750" style="display:none">One of my favorite books of all time! What Do People Do All Day? is a picture book written and illustrated by Richard Scarry. It’s appropriate for children aged 3-7. In 2012, the book won the Scholastic Parent and Child 100 Greatest Books for Kids. The pages show the town of Busytown and the places people go and work such as a paper mill, construction site, and hospital. The pictures are incredibly detailed and full of recognizable Richard Scarry characters. <br /><br />There are so many ways in which to utilize this book. Kids can learn about occupations and imagine themselves growing up and becoming a home builder, farmer, or fire fighter. Children can explore the experience of certain life events such as being a patient in a hospital. Readers can also discover how things are made such as paper from lumber. Also, the pictures of Lowly Worm on each page can be used for a game of “Where’s Waldo.” Additionally, the book can be read in parts with a focus on only one or two places or occupations instead of reading it traditionally from beginning to end. Lastly, children will be introduced to the concept of just how important every job is to a society. With so much important information and so many uses, in addition to its pure entertainment value, this book deserves a top rating. Reviewed 8/9/17</span>
  <a data-text-id="12020507696607745750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7KfP+e7sz/E2tHem4sicho8KxZrJcawejurRCnCTYBEGOub+CV3UR2h3s2i2WRgPoHGWFaoR/pmNSfv6e/TRmg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qOG0BqRrGeirmNk7+XUcVyfih5y5R6Anplojg+o9G/lCfJ0BQ9oCXvVbHfWt5JjeCJnUE9on8qCl+Qlz4Vqqcg==')})
  }

Mike and his trusty steam shovel, Mary Anne, dig deep canals for boats to travel through, cut <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12040093346007079490\" style=\"display:none\">A modern classic that no child should miss. Since it was first published in 1939, Mike Mulligan and His Steam Shovel has delighted generations of children. Mike and his trusty steam shovel, Mary Anne, dig deep canals for boats to travel through, cut mountain passes for trains, and hollow out cellars for city skyscrapers -- the very symbol of industrial America. But with progress come new machines, and soon the inseparable duo are out of work. Mike believes that Mary Anne can dig as much in a day as one hundred men can dig in a week, and the two have one last chance to prove it and save Mary Anne from the scrap heap. What happens next in the small town of Popperville is a testament to their friendship, and to old-fashioned hard work and ingenuity.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12040093346007079490\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18350209354611519153">RICHARD SCARRY is one of the world's best-loved children's authors EVER! In his extraordinary career, Scarry illustrated over 150 books, many of which have never been out of print. His books have sold over 100 million copies around the world, and are currently published in over twenty languages. No other illustrator has shown such a lively interest in the words and concepts of early childhood. Ric</span>
  <span id="freeText18350209354611519153" style="display:none">RICHARD SCARRY is one of the world's best-loved children's authors EVER! In his extraordinary career, Scarry illustrated over 150 books, many of which have never been out of print. His books have sold over 100 million copies around the world, and are currently published in over twenty languages. No other illustrator has shown such a lively interest in the words and concepts of early childhood. Richard Scarry was posthumously awarded a Lifetime Achievement Award from the Society of Illustrators in 2012.</span>
